I like the time release formula which is touted to work round the clock. When I consistently use this skincare kit, my skin always seems clear, but the toner can be a bit dehydrating if I don't apply a noncomedogenic hydrating cream after cleansing and before toning.<br />Be sure to check the date on the box to receive product with maximum efficacy.<br />I'm a huge advocate of the Proactiv Original System, but reviewing University Medical 24 Hour ClearIng System as well since I've tried both and they seem to be similar.<br />Proactiv skincare has always left my skin blemish free for as long as I've used it. Given my experience with skincare, benzoyl peroxide in a low dosage is the only product which seems to work for me long-term.<br />The Proactiv \\"gentle\\", salicylic acid based system proved ineffective for my skin. I should note that with the Original system, I have found it necessary to apply a hydrating cream such as Cetaphil moisturizing cream after cleansing/prior to application of toner in order to offset the potentially dehydrating effects of the toner. I'd found that when I had applied the toner to dry skin right after cleansing, my skin would wind up dehydrated or parched. This is the case even if I only use the system once per day in the evening. If I apply the system 2x day I have found that my skin gets especially dehydrated and flaky where makeup application would be a problem.<br />As the years passed, I started to get interested in trying out skincare with anti-aging benefits. I'd always have the concern in the back of my mind that the products could contribute to breakouts or not keep my skin clear, but I've tried nevertheless.<br />Derm Exclusive seemed to be neutral. I didn't notice any unusual or timely breakouts from use of the product line, but Kardashian's Perfect Skin cleanser always seemed to cause pimples on my skin anytime I've used it. I'm contributing it to their cleanser, although I suppose it could be the toner as well as this product was used some of the time when the cleanser had been used, but breakouts occurred even when their toner was not used.<br />I ran out of Proactiv and Derm Exclusive cleansers so I had decided to try the Perfect Skin cleanser again, but much to my dismay, instant pimples the following morning!! Ugh. I therefore decided to purchase both University Medical Original 24 Hour Clearing System and the Sensitive Skin as an immediate measure since these are available at local pharmacies. I am considering applying the Original in the evening and the Sensitive formula during the AM, but I'm very much concerned about the amount of ALCOHOL that's in the Renewing Toner of the Original System, listed as the second and seventh ingredient while glycolic acid is listed as the eighth. In the Proactiv toner, there's no alcohol and glycolic acid is listed as the second ingredient. Alcohol is known to strip the skin of it's natural lipids and pH balance. When you strip the skin you can cause the skin to fall out of balance where it overproduces oil to compensate for stripping it's natural lipids. This can lead to more breakouts once you moisturize in order to offset the dryness and dehydration. Alcohol also dries the skin and emphasizes fine lines. I'm also concerned that stripping the skin with alcohol leads to dehydration, flaking and possible emphasis of fine lines since hydration and propr balance are especially important for mature skin. My skin is not oily by any means, it tends to be combination or sensitive/acne-prone in that the wrong ingredients (mineral oil, lanolin, parabens, excess oils, non-comedogenic and pore-clogging ingredients) will make me break out, cause redness, chapping, dehydration and flaking.<br />I've noticed that Proactiv uses glycolic acid in it's toner. Their toner was excellent for my skin. It would make it appear more clear, bright and even-toned. Some even consider glycolic acid an anti-aging ingredient, because it brightens dull skin and aids in gentle exfoliation while keeping the pores free of debris. The choice of alcohol as the second and seventh ingredients in the University Medical toner to dilute the product and place glycolic acid as the eighth ingredient (UM) instead of the second ingredient (Proactiv) would explain the price differential as alcohol is a cheap ingredient, but it's also an inferior ingredient. I'm hoping that one of the representatives of University Medical will read this review and consider forwarding the comment to their Research & Development (R&D) Dept. to consider an alcohol-free reformulation of the toner in the Original 3 pc. 24 Hour Clearing System.<br />If you are experiencing dehydration, dryness, tightness, or flakiness of the skin, please consider sending University Medical Customer Service an email via their website explaining your side effects and expressing a desire in an alcohol-free based toner which instead includes well-received and regarded ingredients, such as salicylic, glycolic, AHA, fruit acids, glycerin, sodium PCA, aloe, rose, witch hazel, etc.. have all been shown in proper combination to help to clear pores, increase cell turnover and exfoliation, soothe, hydrate and have anti-aging benefits. Alcohol is a cheap ingredient known to strip and dehydrate the skin and water down the potency of the other ingredients.<br />I will keep you posted on whether the University Medical products are effective as they've just been purchased. I will provide benefit of the doubt for now and provide a 3-4 star rating pending followup.<br />I'd appreciate any feedback you may have regarding using the kits on adult skin that doesn't have bad breakouts, because the skin is managed in a way to keep it clear. The morning following application of Perfect Skin cleanser, my skin had tiny pimples on the cheeks and a hive type of blemish on my chin. Use of Proactiv original system (low dosages of benzoyl peroxide) seems to keep my skin clear.   135. As a person who is in his mid-late 20's who has struggled with acne for most of my life, I have some information that may be useful as I have researched and tried everything, including prescriptions. If a person is sensitive to Benzoyl Peroxide, you should not use this product. With all Benzoyl Peroxide products, it will irritate the skin of anybody sensitive to it. This doesn't exactly mean that you have sensitive skin, but that you are sensitive to this medication. You would also have this problem with other over the counter medications containing this drug. Now to the good stuff. Read and follow the instructions. Step 1 is the cleanser, so massage it into your face and wash it off. Step 2 is the toner, so apply it with a cotton PAD (not a BALL). After the toner has dried, apply step 3 with another cotton pad in a LIGHT layer. Now for the final step which is on the step 3 bottle as a recommendation. I'd actually consider this a requirement. USE AN SPF MOISTURIZER. I use Neutrogena's oil-free moisturizer with SPF-15. This is going to greatly reduce any redness and dryness. You will probably be sorry if you do not use a moisturizer with this as Benzoyl Peroxide is very drying and irritating. The step 3 lotion is not a moisturizer. Again, read and follow the instructions and use a moisturizer. I can only speak from experience, but following this method will give you the most amount of effectiveness and the least amount of side effects.

Whenever that happened, I stopped using the product for a day or two, and moisturized religiously until my skin recovered. As my skin got used to the product, those symptoms disappeared entirely. I am not sure if I would recommend this product to people with sensitive skin, but if you can handle the benzoyl peroxide and you have stubborn acne, this is a great product.<br /><br />A few notes on using the product:<br /><br />(1) When using the cleanser during Step 1, I massage it into my skin for at least 30 seconds before rinsing it off, so that it has time to penetrate the surface. It's especially important to hit the spots that you aren't going to use repair lotion on, so those areas can some daily exposure to the benzoyl peroxide medication. I noticed that when I didn't do this, I would occasionally get acne where I didn't expect it, since I wasn't using the repair lotion on those areas.<br /><br />(2) Early on, I found that the skin toner runs out very quickly and the high alcohol content sometimes stung and dried out my skin. Now, I use Thayer's Witch Hazel for Step 2 instead of the AcneFree toner. Thayer's is alcohol free, inexpensive right here on Amazon, and much gentler on my skin. I love it!<br /><br />(3) I still use repair lotion on \\"trouble areas\\" even though I don't have any acne at this point. I find that applying the lotion to those acne-prone areas keeps any new blemishes from forming. Preventative care is much better than dealing with acne once it develops!<br /><br />(4) At night, I skip Step 3 and instead use Neutrogena Anti-Blemish, Anti-Wrinkle cream. It's got retinol and salicylic acid, which help keep my skin clear but don't run the risk of bleaching out my sheets and pillowcases. It also gives my skin a break from the benzoyl peroxide, which I think has helped with my prior sensitivity to BP.<br /><br />** 12/30/2011 UPDATE: It's been about six months since my original review, and my skin is still smooth and completely acne-free. This product really works wonders. Not only does it keep the blemishes away, but the witch hazel keeps my face looking fresh and even colored.
